</td></tr><tr style="display:none"><th colspan="2">
</th></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Fudan University</b> (<b>FDU</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Public_university" title="Public university">national public university</a> in <a href="/wiki/Yangpu,_Shanghai" title="Yangpu, Shanghai">Yangpu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shanghai" title="Shanghai">Shanghai</a>, China. It is affiliated with the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Education_(China)" title="Ministry of Education (China)">Ministry of Education</a> and is co-funded with the <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Municipal_People%27s_Government" title="Shanghai Municipal People&#39;s Government">Shanghai Municipal Government</a>. The university is part of <a href="/wiki/Project_211" title="Project 211">Project 211</a>, <a href="/wiki/Project_985" title="Project 985">Project 985</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Double_First-Class_Construction" title="Double First-Class Construction">Double First-Class Construction</a>.  
</p><p>The university was originally founded by the Chinese <a href="/wiki/Jesuits" title="Jesuits">Jesuit</a> priest <a href="/wiki/Ma_Xiangbo" title="Ma Xiangbo">Ma Xiangbo</a> in 1905. It is a member of the <a href="/wiki/C9_League" title="C9 League">C9 League</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="History">History</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fudan_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="1905–1917:_college-preparatory_school"><span id="1905.E2.80.931917:_college-preparatory_school"></span>1905–1917: college-preparatory school</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fudan_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: 1905–1917: college-preparatory school"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The university traces its origins to Fudan College, established in 1905 by Chinese Jesuit priest <a href="/wiki/Ma_Xiangbo" title="Ma Xiangbo">Ma Xiangbo</a>. Prior to founding Fudan, Ma had established <a href="/wiki/Aurora_University_(Shanghai)" title="Aurora University (Shanghai)">Aurora College</a>, where the <a href="/wiki/Society_of_Jesus" class="mw-redirect" title="Society of Jesus">Society of Jesus</a> frequently opposed and intervened in student movements. This led Ma to create a new institution, Fudan College, as a preparatory school for higher education with government funding, offering three-year education for general or specialised tracks.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page: 58-60">&#58;&#8202;58-60&#8202;</span></sup> After the <a href="/wiki/1911_Revolution" title="1911 Revolution">1911 Revolution</a>, Fudan continued to offer general rather than specialised education.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page: 63">&#58;&#8202;63&#8202;</span></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="1917–1941:_private_university"><span id="1917.E2.80.931941:_private_university"></span>1917–1941: private university</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fudan_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1917–1941: private university"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Fudan became a private university in 1917, establishing specialised departments including Chinese literature, foreign literature, banking, business and administration, economics, politics, civil engineering and psychology.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page: 63">&#58;&#8202;63&#8202;</span></sup> In 1921, university preparatory education was ended and the university began to adopt an American-styled credit and elective system, per a national policy.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_4-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page: 69">&#58;&#8202;69&#8202;</span></sup> In 1928, Fudan was registered with the Ministry of Education of the newly founded Nationalist government. In 1929, the university was organised into four faculties, namely Liberal Arts, Science, Law and Commerce. In 1937, it moved to Chongqing due to the outbreak of the Second Sino-Japanese War.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_4-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page: 71">&#58;&#8202;71&#8202;</span></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="1941–1949:_national_university"><span id="1941.E2.80.931949:_national_university"></span>1941–1949: national university</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fudan_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1941–1949: national university"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In 1941, with the approval from the Nationalist government, the university was transformed from a private university to a national university, which allowed the government to control Fudan's major posts, including the president, provost and dean. In early 1946, the university returned to Shanghai.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_4-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page: 71">&#58;&#8202;71&#8202;</span></sup> In China under Chiang Kai-shek and the Kuomintang, Fudan University was tasked with providing a Western-style education to Chinese students to support the country's economic reconstruction efforts.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_4-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page: 75">&#58;&#8202;75&#8202;</span></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="1949–1976:_Mao_Zedong_era"><span id="1949.E2.80.931976:_Mao_Zedong_era"></span>1949–1976: Mao Zedong era</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fudan_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 1949–1976: Mao Zedong era"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In 1949, the university was taken over by the Shanghai Military Control Commission of the Chinese Communist Party (CCP), as the CCP defeated the Kuomintang in the Chinese civil war.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_4-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page: 77">&#58;&#8202;77&#8202;</span></sup> By 1952, the CCP remodelled the Chinese higher education based on the Soviet model, leading to the inclusion of Communist ideology in Fudan's educational offerings.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_4-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page: 79">&#58;&#8202;79&#8202;</span></sup> Fudan was transformed into a Soviet-style comprehensive university, with departments of arts and science of other universities merged into Fudan, leaving Fudan the only university to provide basic science and arts in Shanghai.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_4-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page: 81">&#58;&#8202;81&#8202;</span></sup> In China under Mao Zedong, Fudan University was tasked with transmitting socialist values to further the agenda of the CCP.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_4-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page: 78">&#58;&#8202;78&#8202;</span></sup> During the Cultural Revolution, the teaching at Fudan was completely halted due to political turmoils.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_4-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page: 80">&#58;&#8202;80&#8202;</span></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="1976_to_present">1976 to present</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fudan_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 1976 to present"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In 2000, Fudan University merged with Shanghai Medical University, which was founded as the Fourth National Chungshan University School of Medicine in 1927, to form the new Fudan University.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2019, Fudan University changed its constitution, removing the phrase "academic independence and freedom of thought" (學術獨立和思想自由) and including a "pledge to follow the Communist party's leadership" (學校堅持中國共產黨的領導), leading to protests among the students.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It also said that Fudan University had to "equip its teachers and employees" with "<a href="/wiki/Xi_Jinping_Thought" title="Xi Jinping Thought">Xi Jinping Thought</a>", leading to concerns about the diminishing academic freedom of Fudan.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The university set up a 1 billion yuan fund of funds for start up innovation in 2023 as well as launching what it claims to be China’s largest cloud-based scientific research computing platform CFFF.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Fourth_Orb%C3%A1n_Government" title="Fourth Orbán Government">Hungarian government</a> made an agreement to open the first campus of Fudan University outside China in <a href="/wiki/Budapest" title="Budapest">Budapest</a> in 2024.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The expansion would cost 540 billion HUF, of which 450 billion would be paid by the Hungarian state from a Chinese loan. The construction would be mainly done by Chinese companies.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Hungarian education professionals and politicians denounced the investment, citing economics, higher education and national security concerns.<sup id="cite_ref-Telex_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Telex-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Campus">Campus</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fudan_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Campus"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Fudan-xianghuitang.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Fudan-xianghuitang.jpg/250px-Fudan-xianghuitang.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="188" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Fudan-xianghuitang.jpg/500px-Fudan-xianghuitang.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a><figcaption>Xianghui Auditorium</figcaption></figure>
<p>Fudan has five undergraduate colleges – Zhide (<span title="Chinese-language text"><span lang="zh">志德</span></span>), Tengfei (<span title="Chinese-language text"><span lang="zh-Hans">腾飞</span></span>), Keqing (<span title="Chinese-language text"><span lang="zh">克卿</span></span>), Renzhong (<span title="Chinese-language text"><span lang="zh-Hans">任重</span></span>), and Xide (<span title="Chinese-language text"><span lang="zh">希德</span></span>).  
</p><p>The university has four campuses in Shanghai – Handan (<span title="Chinese-language text"><span lang="zh-Hans">邯郸</span></span>), Fenglin (<span title="Chinese-language text"><span lang="zh-Hans">枫林</span></span>), Zhangjiang (<span title="Chinese-language text"><span lang="zh-Hans">张江</span></span>), and Jiangwan (<span title="Chinese-language text"><span lang="zh-Hans">江湾</span></span>) – that share the same central administration. It also has 17 affiliated hospitals. 
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Academic_profile">Academic profile</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fudan_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Academic profile"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="International_links">International links</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fudan_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: International links"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>As of 2024,<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Fudan_University&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> Fudan has joint MBA programs in the School of Management with <a href="/wiki/MIT_Sloan_School_of_Management" title="MIT Sloan School of Management">MIT Sloan School of Management</a> in the US (since 1996, leading to a Fudan degree), <a href="/wiki/BI_Norwegian_Business_School" title="BI Norwegian Business School">BI Norwegian Business School</a> in Norway (since 1996, leading to a BI Norwegian Business School degree), the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Hong_Kong" title="University of Hong Kong">University of Hong Kong</a> in Hong Kong (leading to a University of Hong Kong degree), and <a href="/wiki/Washington_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Washington University">Washington University</a> in the US (leading to a Washington University degree).<sup id="cite_ref-international_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-international-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> There are also a double degree in international management with <a href="/wiki/Bocconi_University" title="Bocconi University">Bocconi University</a> and <a href="/wiki/Luiss_University" title="Luiss University">Luiss University</a> in Italy (since 2005, leading to a master's in international management from one of the Italian universities), an executive MBA with <a href="/wiki/National_Taiwan_University" title="National Taiwan University">National Taiwan University</a>, and a global master's in management with <a href="/wiki/London_Business_School" title="London Business School">London Business School</a> (leading to degrees from both institutions).<sup id="cite_ref-international_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-international-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Fudan University School of Economics has had a partnership with <a href="/wiki/Durham_University_Business_School" title="Durham University Business School">Durham University Business School</a> in England to deliver a <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Business_Administration" title="Doctor of Business Administration">Doctor of Business Administration</a> (DBA) degree awarded by <a href="/wiki/Durham_University" title="Durham University">Durham University</a> since 2006, with the first students starting in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> As of 2024,<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Fudan_University&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> Fudan remains the main location, but some elements of the course are also delivered at Durham and in <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">San Francisco</a>, USA.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Fudan, <a href="/wiki/Korea_University_Business_School" title="Korea University Business School">Korea University Business School</a> in Korea, and the <a href="/wiki/National_University_of_Singapore" title="National University of Singapore">National University of Singapore</a> in Singapore have collaborated on the <a href="/wiki/S3_Asia_MBA" title="S3 Asia MBA">S3 Asia MBA</a> since 2008, with students spending six months at each of the institutions.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Fudan students receive a dual degree from Fudan and one of the other universities in the collaboration.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>

</div><div style="clear: both"></div></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Research_output_rankings">Research output rankings</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fudan_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Research output rankings"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Regarding research output in natural science and life science, the <a href="/wiki/Nature_Index" title="Nature Index">Nature Index</a> Research Leaders 2024 ranked Fudan the No.9 university in the Asia Pacific region, and 12th in the world among the global universities.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The 2024 <a href="/wiki/CWTS_Leiden_Ranking" title="CWTS Leiden Ranking">CWTS Leiden Ranking</a> ranked Fudan 11th in the world based on their publications for the time period 2019–2022.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Notable_alumni">Notable alumni</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fudan_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Notable alumni"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1236090951">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}@media print{body.ns-0 .mw-parser-output .hatnote{display:none!important}}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Fudan_University_people" title="List of Fudan University people">List of Fudan University people</a></div>
<p>Since 1952, Fudan University has a total of 95 academicians alumni, second only to Peking University and Tsinghua University in China.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Fudan's notable alumni include:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Chen_Yinke" title="Chen Yinke">Chen Yinke</a> (1890–1969), historian, linguist, orientalist, politician, and writer.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Chen_Wangdao" title="Chen Wangdao">Chen Wangdao</a> (1891–1977), scholar and educator recognized as the first and only person to translate <i><a href="/wiki/The_Communist_Manifesto" title="The Communist Manifesto">The Communist Manifesto</a></i> into Chinese completely</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Chen_Zhili" title="Chen Zhili">Chen Zhili</a> (born 1942), politician</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Chu_Coching" title="Chu Coching">Chu Coching</a>, <a href="/wiki/Geologist" title="Geologist">geologist</a> and <a href="/wiki/Meteorologist" title="Meteorologist">meteorologist</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/David_Ji" title="David Ji">David Ji</a> (born 1952), Chinese-American electronics entrepreneur who co-founded <a href="/wiki/Apex_Digital" title="Apex Digital">Apex Digital</a>, and  was held against his will in China for months without charges during a business dispute</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kerry_Chen" title="Kerry Chen">Kerry Chen</a>, entrepreneur, founder and CEO of ATRenew</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Yan_Fu" title="Yan Fu">Yan Fu</a>, military officer, newspaper editor, translator, and writer known for introducing <a href="/wiki/Western_culture" title="Western culture">Western ideas</a> to China in the late 19th century</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Yu_Youren" title="Yu Youren">Yu Youren</a>, educator, scholar, calligrapher, and politician</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Wang_Huning" title="Wang Huning">Wang Huning</a> (born 1955), political theorist and a top leader of the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Communist_Party" title="Chinese Communist Party">Chinese Communist Party</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:4_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
